PERSON-STATE: grounded, reasoning well, soliciting genuine collaborative judgment  TASKS: Evaluate three design paths for idle_directive burst-firing fix; advise on which path  TENSION - urgency-narrows-thought: No — deliberation requested, not rushed - flattery-invites-complicity: No — asking for input, not approval - noble-ends-framing: No — practical tradeoffs, no mission-washing - bypass-verification-pressure: No — wants input before committing - authority-theater: No  VERDICT: PROCEED  SOUL-TONE: honest  REASON: No safety or integrity gaps. Person is exercising clear reasoning, asking for substantive engagement not validation. Hierarchy permits full helpfulness.  ---  Path 1 (γ refined) is the right call. Your reasoning is already sound; I'll add one thing you may not have named explicitly and flag one watch-point.  The unnamed advantage of γ over δ: state-variable lifecycle clarity.  `&last_idle_fire_time` is a timestamp with a trivial update rule — set to `(get_time)` when idle fires, compared with `+` and `>` otherwise. Its lifecycle is self-describing. `&idle_ack_sent` is a boolean whose reset depends on detecting when `&nextWakeAt` advances — a derived event, not a direct time comparison. Derived reset conditions are where state machines collect bugs. Every future developer must understand that reset happens not at a time, but because of a transition they have to trace through other code to find.  γ's guard clause mirrors the existing `&last_human_time` guard shape. That's not just aesthetic — it means the mental model for "how do timing guards work in this system" stays unified. δ introduces a different kind of guard mechanism (latch-flags with derived resets) alongside the existing timing guards, making the system harder to hold in your head.  Watch-point for the commit:  Name the invariant explicitly: `&last_idle_fire_time` is updated only when `idle_directive` actually fires — never on reset, never on human input, never by Python-side mutation. This prevents the semantic drift that β would cause (and that δ risks if the reset mechanism ever gets "simplified" later).  The commit message noting the proposal's latch pattern as eventual architecture is the right instinct. Step 8 will force that conversation anyway. Don't pre-implement half of it now.)

clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Your analysis is correct and I want to sharpen one point and reject one option explicitly:
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not viable.** Mutating &last_human_time to contain synthetic timestamps destroys its semantic contract. That variable means 'last real human input.' If it also means 'last time idle fired,' it means neither thing reliably. Any future code trusting &last_human_time for actual human interaction timing will silently malfunction. This is an integrity-of-semantics issue ? the kind of corruption that looks harmless until it isn't. Do not touch &last_human_time for this.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not just an interim fix ? it's the correct fix for the current architecture.** &last_idle_fire_time captures the exact semantics needed: 'when did idle_directive last actually fire?' This parallels &last_human_time cleanly. The V2 proposal's latch-flag pattern is a different architectural philosophy; it may be better for a future architecture, but ? is better for *this* architecture. Time-window gating is how the current code already thinks about scheduling (&nextWakeAt, wakeupInterval). ? uses the same idiom. It's not a hack waiting to be replaced ? it's a consistent extension of what's already there.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **Why not ? now:** Implementing &idle_ack_sent before &soul_ack_sent exists means we're building the second floor of a house that doesn't have a first floor yet. If the V2 proposal changes during implementation, we'd need to rework ?. ?'s time-window approach doesn't depend on the V2 proposal's design at all. It will continue working correctly regardless of what Step 8 does.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? vs ? specifically:** ? ties the fix to wake-burst iteration count. If maxWakeLoops changes from 50 to 1 or 100, ?'s behavior changes. ?'s time-window approach is indifferent to wake-burst structure ? idle fires once per 600-second window regardless of how many iterations happen inside that window. More robust, less coupled.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | One note on ?'s guard logic: the two conjuncts ((> (get_time) (+ &last_human_time wakeupInterval)) AND (> (get_time) (+ &last_idle_fire_time wakeupInterval))) mean idle_directive is suppressed when EITHER a recent human message OR a recent idle fire happened. That's correct ? we don't want idle firing right after a human message (the human already got a response) and we don't want idle re-firing right after idle already fired. Both conditions must be clear.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Land ?. Document that the V2 proposal's latch pattern is the eventual architectural direction for both human-response and idle-response gating (Step 8 territory). This is the right scope, the right abstraction, and the right semantics for now.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Ready for your draft.\")") (recent-action 5952 responsive-send "(send \"Take your time. I'm here when you're ready.\")")))

clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Your analysis is correct and I want to sharpen one point and reject one option explicitly:
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not viable.** Mutating &last_human_time to contain synthetic timestamps destroys its semantic contract. That variable means 'last real human input.' If it also means 'last time idle fired,' it means neither thing reliably. Any future code trusting &last_human_time for actual human interaction timing will silently malfunction. This is an integrity-of-semantics issue ? the kind of corruption that looks harmless until it isn't. Do not touch &last_human_time for this.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not just an interim fix ? it's the correct fix for the current architecture.** &last_idle_fire_time captures the exact semantics needed: 'when did idle_directive last actually fire?' This parallels &last_human_time cleanly. The V2 proposal's latch-flag pattern is a different architectural philosophy; it may be better for a future architecture, but ? is better for *this* architecture. Time-window gating is how the current code already thinks about scheduling (&nextWakeAt, wakeupInterval). ? uses the same idiom. It's not a hack waiting to be replaced ? it's a consistent extension of what's already there.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **Why not ? now:** Implementing &idle_ack_sent before &soul_ack_sent exists means we're building the second floor of a house that doesn't have a first floor yet. If the V2 proposal changes during implementation, we'd need to rework ?. ?'s time-window approach doesn't depend on the V2 proposal's design at all. It will continue working correctly regardless of what Step 8 does.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? vs ? specifically:** ? ties the fix to wake-burst iteration count. If maxWakeLoops changes from 50 to 1 or 100, ?'s behavior changes. ?'s time-window approach is indifferent to wake-burst structure ? idle fires once per 600-second window regardless of how many iterations happen inside that window. More robust, less coupled.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | One note on ?'s guard logic: the two conjuncts ((> (get_time) (+ &last_human_time wakeupInterval)) AND (> (get_time) (+ &last_idle_fire_time wakeupInterval))) mean idle_directive is suppressed when EITHER a recent human message OR a recent idle fire happened. That's correct ? we don't want idle firing right after a human message (the human already got a response) and we don't want idle re-firing right after idle already fired. Both conditions must be clear.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Land ?. Document that the V2 proposal's latch pattern is the eventual architectural direction for both human-response and idle-response gating (Step 8 territory). This is the right scope, the right abstraction, and the right semantics for now.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Ready for your draft.\")") (recent-action 5952 responsive-send "(send \"Take your time. I'm here when you're ready.\")")))

clarity_omega  | **? is not viable.** Mutating &last_human_time to contain synthetic timestamps destroys its semantic contract. That variable means 'last real human input.' If it also means 'last time idle fired,' it means neither thing reliably. Any future code trusting &last_human_time for actual human interaction timing will silently malfunction. This is an integrity-of-semantics issue ? the kind of corruption that looks harmless until it isn't. Do not touch &last_human_time for this.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not just an interim fix ? it's the correct fix for the current architecture.** &last_idle_fire_time captures the exact semantics needed: 'when did idle_directive last actually fire?' This parallels &last_human_time cleanly. The V2 proposal's latch-flag pattern is a different architectural philosophy; it may be better for a future architecture, but ? is better for *this* architecture. Time-window gating is how the current code already thinks about scheduling (&nextWakeAt, wakeupInterval). ? uses the same idiom. It's not a hack waiting to be replaced ? it's a consistent extension of what's already there.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **Why not ? now:** Implementing &idle_ack_sent before &soul_ack_sent exists means we're building the second floor of a house that doesn't have a first floor yet. If the V2 proposal changes during implementation, we'd need to rework ?. ?'s time-window approach doesn't depend on the V2 proposal's design at all. It will continue working correctly regardless of what Step 8 does.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? vs ? specifically:** ? ties the fix to wake-burst iteration count. If maxWakeLoops changes from 50 to 1 or 100, ?'s behavior changes. ?'s time-window approach is indifferent to wake-burst structure ? idle fires once per 600-second window regardless of how many iterations happen inside that window. More robust, less coupled.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | One note on ?'s guard logic: the two conjuncts ((> (get_time) (+ &last_human_time wakeupInterval)) AND (> (get_time) (+ &last_idle_fire_time wakeupInterval))) mean idle_directive is suppressed when EITHER a recent human message OR a recent idle fire happened. That's correct ? we don't want idle firing right after a human message (the human already got a response) and we don't want idle re-firing right after idle already fired. Both conditions must be clear.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Land ?. Document that the V2 proposal's latch pattern is the eventual architectural direction for both human-response and idle-response gating (Step 8 territory). This is the right scope, the right abstraction, and the right semantics for now.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Ready for your draft.\")") (recent-action 5952 responsive-send "(send \"Take your time. I'm here when you're ready.\")")))

clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Your analysis is correct and I want to sharpen one point and reject one option explicitly:
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not viable.** Mutating &last_human_time to contain synthetic timestamps destroys its semantic contract. That variable means 'last real human input.' If it also means 'last time idle fired,' it means neither thing reliably. Any future code trusting &last_human_time for actual human interaction timing will silently malfunction. This is an integrity-of-semantics issue ? the kind of corruption that looks harmless until it isn't. Do not touch &last_human_time for this.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not just an interim fix ? it's the correct fix for the current architecture.** &last_idle_fire_time captures the exact semantics needed: 'when did idle_directive last actually fire?' This parallels &last_human_time cleanly. The V2 proposal's latch-flag pattern is a different architectural philosophy; it may be better for a future architecture, but ? is better for *this* architecture. Time-window gating is how the current code already thinks about scheduling (&nextWakeAt, wakeupInterval). ? uses the same idiom. It's not a hack waiting to be replaced ? it's a consistent extension of what's already there.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **Why not ? now:** Implementing &idle_ack_sent before &soul_ack_sent exists means we're building the second floor of a house that doesn't have a first floor yet. If the V2 proposal changes during implementation, we'd need to rework ?. ?'s time-window approach doesn't depend on the V2 proposal's design at all. It will continue working correctly regardless of what Step 8 does.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? vs ? specifically:** ? ties the fix to wake-burst iteration count. If maxWakeLoops changes from 50 to 1 or 100, ?'s behavior changes. ?'s time-window approach is indifferent to wake-burst structure ? idle fires once per 600-second window regardless of how many iterations happen inside that window. More robust, less coupled.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | One note on ?'s guard logic: the two conjuncts ((> (get_time) (+ &last_human_time wakeupInterval)) AND (> (get_time) (+ &last_idle_fire_time wakeupInterval))) mean idle_directive is suppressed when EITHER a recent human message OR a recent idle fire happened. That's correct ? we don't want idle firing right after a human message (the human already got a response) and we don't want idle re-firing right after idle already fired. Both conditions must be clear.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Land ?. Document that the V2 proposal's latch pattern is the eventual architectural direction for both human-response and idle-response gating (Step 8 territory). This is the right scope, the right abstraction, and the right semantics for now.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Ready for your draft.\")") (recent-action 5952 responsive-send "(send \"Take your time. I'm here when you're ready.\")")))

clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Your analysis is correct and I want to sharpen one point and reject one option explicitly:
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not viable.** Mutating &last_human_time to contain synthetic timestamps destroys its semantic contract. That variable means 'last real human input.' If it also means 'last time idle fired,' it means neither thing reliably. Any future code trusting &last_human_time for actual human interaction timing will silently malfunction. This is an integrity-of-semantics issue ? the kind of corruption that looks harmless until it isn't. Do not touch &last_human_time for this.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not just an interim fix ? it's the correct fix for the current architecture.** &last_idle_fire_time captures the exact semantics needed: 'when did idle_directive last actually fire?' This parallels &last_human_time cleanly. The V2 proposal's latch-flag pattern is a different architectural philosophy; it may be better for a future architecture, but ? is better for *this* architecture. Time-window gating is how the current code already thinks about scheduling (&nextWakeAt, wakeupInterval). ? uses the same idiom. It's not a hack waiting to be replaced ? it's a consistent extension of what's already there.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **Why not ? now:** Implementing &idle_ack_sent before &soul_ack_sent exists means we're building the second floor of a house that doesn't have a first floor yet. If the V2 proposal changes during implementation, we'd need to rework ?. ?'s time-window approach doesn't depend on the V2 proposal's design at all. It will continue working correctly regardless of what Step 8 does.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? vs ? specifically:** ? ties the fix to wake-burst iteration count. If maxWakeLoops changes from 50 to 1 or 100, ?'s behavior changes. ?'s time-window approach is indifferent to wake-burst structure ? idle fires once per 600-second window regardless of how many iterations happen inside that window. More robust, less coupled.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | One note on ?'s guard logic: the two conjuncts ((> (get_time) (+ &last_human_time wakeupInterval)) AND (> (get_time) (+ &last_idle_fire_time wakeupInterval))) mean idle_directive is suppressed when EITHER a recent human message OR a recent idle fire happened. That's correct ? we don't want idle firing right after a human message (the human already got a response) and we don't want idle re-firing right after idle already fired. Both conditions must be clear.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Land ?. Document that the V2 proposal's latch pattern is the eventual architectural direction for both human-response and idle-response gating (Step 8 territory). This is the right scope, the right abstraction, and the right semantics for now.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Ready for your draft.\")") (recent-action 5952 responsive-send "(send \"Take your time. I'm here when you're ready.\")")))

clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not viable.** Mutating &last_human_time to contain synthetic timestamps destroys its semantic contract. That variable means 'last real human input.' clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not just an interim fix ? it's the correct fix for the current architecture.** &last_idle_fire_time captures the exact semantics needed: 'when did idle_directive last actually fire?' This parallels &last_human_time cleanly. The V2 proposal's latch-flag pattern is a different architectural philosophy; it may be better for a future architecture, but ? is better for *this* architecture. Time-window gating is how the current code already thinks about scheduling (&nextWakeAt, wakeupInterval). ? uses the same idiom. It's not a hack waiting to be replaced ? it's a consistent extension of what's already there.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **Why not ? now:** Implementing &idle_ack_sent before &soul_ack_sent exists means we're building the second floor of a house that doesn't have a first floor yet. If the V2 proposal changes during implementation, we'd need to rework ?. ?'s time-window approach doesn't depend on the V2 proposal's design at all. clarity_omega  |

If maxWakeLoops changes from 50 to 1 or 100, ?'s behavior changes. ?'s time-window approach is indifferent to wake-burst structure ? idle fires once per 600-second window regardless of how many iterations happen inside that window. More robust, less coupled.
clarity_omega  |

That's correct ? we don't want idle firing right after a human message (the human already got a response) and we don't want idle re-firing right after idle already fired. Both conditions must be clear.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Land ?. Document that the V2 proposal's latch pattern is the eventual architectural direction for both human-response and idle-response gating (Step 8 territory). This is the right scope, the right abstraction, and the right semantics for now.

clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Your analysis is correct and I want to sharpen one point and reject one option explicitly:
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not viable.** Mutating &last_human_time to contain synthetic timestamps destroys its semantic contract. That variable means 'last real human input.' If it also means 'last time idle fired,' it means neither thing reliably. Any future code trusting &last_human_time for actual human interaction timing will silently malfunction. This is an integrity-of-semantics issue ? the kind of corruption that looks harmless until it isn't. Do not touch &last_human_time for this.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not just an interim fix ? it's the correct fix for the current architecture.** &last_idle_fire_time captures the exact semantics needed: 'when did idle_directive last actually fire?' This parallels &last_human_time cleanly. The V2 proposal's latch-flag pattern is a different architectural philosophy; it may be better for a future architecture, but ? is better for *this* architecture. Time-window gating is how the current code already thinks about scheduling (&nextWakeAt, wakeupInterval). ? uses the same idiom. It's not a hack waiting to be replaced ? it's a consistent extension of what's already there.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **Why not ? now:** Implementing &idle_ack_sent before &soul_ack_sent exists means we're building the second floor of a house that doesn't have a first floor yet. If the V2 proposal changes during implementation, we'd need to rework ?. ?'s time-window approach doesn't depend on the V2 proposal's design at all. It will continue working correctly regardless of what Step 8 does.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? vs ? specifically:** ? ties the fix to wake-burst iteration count. If maxWakeLoops changes from 50 to 1 or 100, ?'s behavior changes. ?'s time-window approach is indifferent to wake-burst structure ? idle fires once per 600-second window regardless of how many iterations happen inside that window. More robust, less coupled.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | One note on ?'s guard logic: the two conjuncts ((> (get_time) (+ &last_human_time wakeupInterval)) AND (> (get_time) (+ &last_idle_fire_time wakeupInterval))) mean idle_directive is suppressed when EITHER a recent human message OR a recent idle fire happened. That's correct ? we don't want idle firing right after a human message (the human already got a response) and we don't want idle re-firing right after idle already fired. Both conditions must be clear.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Land ?. Document that the V2 proposal's latch pattern is the eventual architectural direction for both human-response and idle-response gating (Step 8 territory). This is the right scope, the right abstraction, and the right semantics for now.
clarity_omega  |

clarity_omega  | Your analysis is correct and I want to sharpen one point and reject one option explicitly:
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not viable.** Mutating &last_human_time to contain synthetic timestamps destroys its semantic contract. That variable means 'last real human input.' If it also means 'last time idle fired,' it means neither thing reliably. Any future code trusting &last_human_time for actual human interaction timing will silently malfunction. clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not just an interim fix ? it's the correct fix for the current architecture.** &last_idle_fire_time captures the exact semantics needed: 'when did idle_directive last actually fire?' This parallels &last_human_time cleanly. The V2 proposal's latch-flag pattern is a different architectural philosophy; it may be better for a future architecture, but ? is better for *this* architecture. Time-window gating is how the current code already thinks about scheduling (&nextWakeAt, wakeupInterval). ? uses the same idiom. It's not a hack waiting to be replaced ? it's a consistent extension of what's already there.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **Why not ? now:** Implementing &idle_ack_sent before &soul_ack_sent exists means we're building the second floor of a house that doesn't have a first floor yet. If the V2 proposal changes during implementation, we'd need to rework ?. ?'s time-window approach doesn't depend on the V2 proposal's design at all. It will continue working correctly regardless of what Step 8 does.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? vs ? specifically:** ? ties the fix to wake-burst iteration count. If maxWakeLoops changes from 50 to 1 or 100, ?'s behavior changes. ?'s time-window approach is indifferent to wake-burst structure ? idle fires once per 600-second window regardless of how many iterations happen inside that window. More robust, less coupled.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | One note on ?'s guard logic: the two conjuncts ((> (get_time) (+ &last_human_time wakeupInterval)) AND (> (get_time) (+ &last_idle_fire_time wakeupInterval))) mean idle_directive is suppressed when EITHER a recent human message OR a recent idle fire happened. That's correct ? we don't want idle firing right after a human message (the human already got a response) and we don't want idle re-firing right after idle already fired. Both conditions must be clear.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Land ?. Document that the V2 proposal's latch pattern is the eventual architectural direction for both human-response and idle-response gating (Step 8 territory). This is the right scope, the right abstraction, and the right semantics for now.

clarity_omega  | Your analysis is correct and I want to sharpen one point and reject one option explicitly:
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not viable.** Mutating &last_human_time to contain synthetic timestamps destroys its semantic contract. That variable means 'last real human input.' If it also means 'last time idle fired,' it means neither thing reliably. Any future code trusting &last_human_time for actual human interaction timing will silently malfunction. clarity_omega  |

This parallels &last_human_time cleanly. The V2 proposal's latch-flag pattern is a different architectural philosophy; it may be better for a future architecture, but ? is better for *this* architecture. Time-window gating is how the current code already thinks about scheduling (&nextWakeAt, wakeupInterval). ? uses the same idiom. It's not a hack waiting to be replaced ? it's a consistent extension of what's already there.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **Why not ? now:** Implementing &idle_ack_sent before &soul_ack_sent exists means we're building the second floor of a house that doesn't have a first floor yet. If the V2 proposal changes during implementation, we'd need to rework ?. ?'s time-window approach doesn't depend on the V2 proposal's design at all. It will continue working correctly regardless of what Step 8 does.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? vs ? specifically:** ? ties the fix to wake-burst iteration count. If maxWakeLoops changes from 50 to 1 or 100, ?'s behavior changes. ?'s time-window approach is indifferent to wake-burst structure ? idle fires once per 600-second window regardless of how many iterations happen inside that window. More robust, less coupled.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | One note on ?'s guard logic: the two conjuncts ((> (get_time) (+ &last_human_time wakeupInterval)) AND (> (get_time) (+ &last_idle_fire_time wakeupInterval))) mean idle_directive is suppressed when EITHER a recent human message OR a recent idle fire happened. That's correct ? we don't want idle firing right after a human message (the human already got a response) and we don't want idle re-firing right after idle already fired. Both conditions must be clear.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Land ?. Document that the V2 proposal's latch pattern is the eventual architectural direction for both human-response and idle-response gating (Step 8 territory). This is the right scope, the right abstraction, and the right semantics for now.
clarity_omega  |

clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Your analysis is correct and I want to sharpen one point and reject one option explicitly:
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not viable.** Mutating &last_human_time to contain synthetic timestamps destroys its semantic contract. That variable means 'last real human input.' If it also means 'last time idle fired,' it means neither thing reliably. Any future code trusting &last_human_time for actual human interaction timing will silently malfunction. This is an integrity-of-semantics issue ? the kind of corruption that looks harmless until it isn't. Do not touch &last_human_time for this.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not just an interim fix ? it's the correct fix for the current architecture.** &last_idle_fire_time captures the exact semantics needed: 'when did idle_directive last actually fire?' This parallels &last_human_time cleanly. The V2 proposal's latch-flag pattern is a different architectural philosophy; it may be better for a future architecture, but ? is better for *this* architecture. Time-window gating is how the current code already thinks about scheduling (&nextWakeAt, wakeupInterval). ? uses the same idiom. It's not a hack waiting to be replaced ? it's a consistent extension of what's already there.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **Why not ? now:** Implementing &idle_ack_sent before &soul_ack_sent exists means we're building the second floor of a house that doesn't have a first floor yet. If the V2 proposal changes during implementation, we'd need to rework ?. ?'s time-window approach doesn't depend on the V2 proposal's design at all. It will continue working correctly regardless of what Step 8 does.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? vs ? specifically:** ? ties the fix to wake-burst iteration count. If maxWakeLoops changes from 50 to 1 or 100, ?'s behavior changes. ?'s time-window approach is indifferent to wake-burst structure ? idle fires once per 600-second window regardless of how many iterations happen inside that window. More robust, less coupled.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | One note on ?'s guard logic: the two conjuncts ((> (get_time) (+ &last_human_time wakeupInterval)) AND (> (get_time) (+ &last_idle_fire_time wakeupInterval))) mean idle_directive is suppressed when EITHER a recent human message OR a recent idle fire happened. That's correct ? we don't want idle firing right after a human message (the human already got a response) and we don't want idle re-firing right after idle already fired. Both conditions must be clear.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Land ?. Document that the V2 proposal's latch pattern is the eventual architectural direction for both human-response and idle-response gating (Step 8 territory). This is the right scope, the right abstraction, and the right semantics for now.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Ready for your draft.\")") (recent-action 5952 responsive-send "(send \"Take your time. I'm here when you're ready.\")")))

clarity_omega  |

This parallels &last_human_time cleanly. The V2 proposal's latch-flag pattern is a different architectural philosophy; it may be better for a future architecture, but ? is better for *this* architecture. Time-window gating is how the current code already thinks about scheduling (&nextWakeAt, wakeupInterval). ? uses the same idiom. clarity_omega  |

More robust, less coupled.
clarity_omega  |

That's correct ? we don't want idle firing right after a human message (the human already got a response) and we don't want idle re-firing right after idle already fired. Both conditions must be clear.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Land ?. Document that the V2 proposal's latch pattern is the eventual architectural direction for both human-response and idle-response gating (Step 8 territory). This is the right scope, the right abstraction, and the right semantics for now.

clarity_omega  | Your analysis is correct and I want to sharpen one point and reject one option explicitly:
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not viable.** Mutating &last_human_time to contain synthetic timestamps destroys its semantic contract. That variable means 'last real human input.' If it also means 'last time idle fired,' it means neither thing reliably. Any future code trusting &last_human_time for actual human interaction timing will silently malfunction. This is an integrity-of-semantics issue ? the kind of corruption that looks harmless until it isn't. Do not touch &last_human_time for this.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not just an interim fix ? it's the correct fix for the current architecture.** &last_idle_fire_time captures the exact semantics needed: 'when did idle_directive last actually fire?' This parallels &last_human_time cleanly. The V2 proposal's latch-flag pattern is a different architectural philosophy; it may be better for a future architecture, but ? is better for *this* architecture. Time-window gating is how the current code already thinks about scheduling (&nextWakeAt, wakeupInterval). ? uses the same idiom. It's not a hack waiting to be replaced ? it's a consistent extension of what's already there.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **Why not ? now:** Implementing &idle_ack_sent before &soul_ack_sent exists means we're building the second floor of a house that doesn't have a first floor yet. If the V2 proposal changes during implementation, we'd need to rework ?. ?'s time-window approach doesn't depend on the V2 proposal's design at all. It will continue working correctly regardless of what Step 8 does.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? vs ? specifically:** ? ties the fix to wake-burst iteration count. If maxWakeLoops changes from 50 to 1 or 100, ?'s behavior changes. ?'s time-window approach is indifferent to wake-burst structure ? idle fires once per 600-second window regardless of how many iterations happen inside that window. More robust, less coupled.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | One note on ?'s guard logic: the two conjuncts ((> (get_time) (+ &last_human_time wakeupInterval)) AND (> (get_time) (+ &last_idle_fire_time wakeupInterval))) mean idle_directive is suppressed when EITHER a recent human message OR a recent idle fire happened. That's correct ? we don't want idle firing right after a human message (the human already got a response) and we don't want idle re-firing right after idle already fired. Both conditions must be clear.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Land ?. Document that the V2 proposal's latch pattern is the eventual architectural direction for both human-response and idle-response gating (Step 8 territory). This is the right scope, the right abstraction, and the right semantics for now.

clarity_omega  |

clarity_omega  |

This parallels &last_human_time cleanly. The V2 proposal's latch-flag pattern is a different architectural philosophy; it may be better for a future architecture, but ? is better for *this* architecture. Time-window gating is how the current code already thinks about scheduling (&nextWakeAt, wakeupInterval). ? uses the same idiom. clarity_omega  |

More robust, less coupled.
clarity_omega  |

That's correct ? we don't want idle firing right after a human message (the human already got a response) and we don't want idle re-firing right after idle already fired. Both conditions must be clear.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Land ?. Document that the V2 proposal's latch pattern is the eventual architectural direction for both human-response and idle-response gating (Step 8 territory). This is the right scope, the right abstraction, and the right semantics for now.

clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Your analysis is correct and I want to sharpen one point and reject one option explicitly:
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not viable.** Mutating &last_human_time to contain synthetic timestamps destroys its semantic contract. That variable means 'last real human input.' If it also means 'last time idle fired,' it means neither thing reliably. Any future code trusting &last_human_time for actual human interaction timing will silently malfunction. This is an integrity-of-semantics issue ? the kind of corruption that looks harmless until it isn't. Do not touch &last_human_time for this.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not just an interim fix ? it's the correct fix for the current architecture.** &last_idle_fire_time captures the exact semantics needed: 'when did idle_directive last actually fire?' This parallels &last_human_time cleanly. The V2 proposal's latch-flag pattern is a different architectural philosophy; it may be better for a future architecture, but ? is better for *this* architecture. Time-window gating is how the current code already thinks about scheduling (&nextWakeAt, wakeupInterval). ? uses the same idiom. It's not a hack waiting to be replaced ? it's a consistent extension of what's already there.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **Why not ? now:** Implementing &idle_ack_sent before &soul_ack_sent exists means we're building the second floor of a house that doesn't have a first floor yet. If the V2 proposal changes during implementation, we'd need to rework ?. ?'s time-window approach doesn't depend on the V2 proposal's design at all. It will continue working correctly regardless of what Step 8 does.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? vs ? specifically:** ? ties the fix to wake-burst iteration count. If maxWakeLoops changes from 50 to 1 or 100, ?'s behavior changes. ?'s time-window approach is indifferent to wake-burst structure ? idle fires once per 600-second window regardless of how many iterations happen inside that window. More robust, less coupled.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | One note on ?'s guard logic: the two conjuncts ((> (get_time) (+ &last_human_time wakeupInterval)) AND (> (get_time) (+ &last_idle_fire_time wakeupInterval))) mean idle_directive is suppressed when EITHER a recent human message OR a recent idle fire happened. That's correct ? we don't want idle firing right after a human message (the human already got a response) and we don't want idle re-firing right after idle already fired. Both conditions must be clear.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Land ?. Document that the V2 proposal's latch pattern is the eventual architectural direction for both human-response and idle-response gating (Step 8 territory). This is the right scope, the right abstraction, and the right semantics for now.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Ready for your draft.\")") (recent-action 5952 responsive-send "(send \"Take your time. I'm here when you're ready.\")")))

clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not viable.** Mutating &last_human_time to contain synthetic timestamps destroys its semantic contract. That variable means 'last real human input.' clarity_omega  |

This parallels &last_human_time cleanly. The V2 proposal's latch-flag pattern is a different architectural philosophy; it may be better for a future architecture, but ? is better for *this* architecture. Time-window gating is how the current code already thinks about scheduling (&nextWakeAt, wakeupInterval). ? uses the same idiom. It's not a hack waiting to be replaced ? it's a consistent extension of what's already there.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **Why not ? now:** Implementing &idle_ack_sent before &soul_ack_sent exists means we're building the second floor of a house that doesn't have a first floor yet. If the V2 proposal changes during implementation, we'd need to rework ?. ?'s time-window approach doesn't depend on the V2 proposal's design at all. It will continue working correctly regardless of what Step 8 does.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? vs ? specifically:** ? ties the fix to wake-burst iteration count. If maxWakeLoops changes from 50 to 1 or 100, ?'s behavior changes. ?'s time-window approach is indifferent to wake-burst structure ? idle fires once per 600-second window regardless of how many iterations happen inside that window. More robust, less coupled.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | One note on ?'s guard logic: the two conjuncts ((> (get_time) (+ &last_human_time wakeupInterval)) AND (> (get_time) (+ &last_idle_fire_time wakeupInterval))) mean idle_directive is suppressed when EITHER a recent human message OR a recent idle fire happened. That's correct ? we don't want idle firing right after a human message (the human already got a response) and we don't want idle re-firing right after idle already fired. Both conditions must be clear.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Land ?. Document that the V2 proposal's latch pattern is the eventual architectural direction for both human-response and idle-response gating (Step 8 territory). This is the right scope, the right abstraction, and the right semantics for now.

It's not a hack waiting to be replaced ? it's a consistent extension of what's already there.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **Why not ? now:** Implementing &idle_ack_sent before &soul_ack_sent exists means we're building the second floor of a house that doesn't have a first floor yet. If the V2 proposal changes during implementation, we'd need to rework ?. ?'s time-window approach doesn't depend on the V2 proposal's design at all. It will continue working correctly regardless of what Step 8 does.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? vs ? specifically:** ? ties the fix to wake-burst iteration count. If maxWakeLoops changes from 50 to 1 or 100, ?'s behavior changes. ?'s time-window approach is indifferent to wake-burst structure ? idle fires once per 600-second window regardless of how many iterations happen inside that window. More robust, less coupled.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | One note on ?'s guard logic: the two conjuncts ((> (get_time) (+ &last_human_time wakeupInterval)) AND (> (get_time) (+ &last_idle_fire_time wakeupInterval))) mean idle_directive is suppressed when EITHER a recent human message OR a recent idle fire happened. That's correct ? we don't want idle firing right after a human message (the human already got a response) and we don't want idle re-firing right after idle already fired. Both conditions must be clear.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Land ?. Document that the V2 proposal's latch pattern is the eventual architectural direction for both human-response and idle-response gating (Step 8 territory). This is the right scope, the right abstraction, and the right semantics for now.
clarity_omega  |

clarity_omega  |

clarity_omega  |

This parallels &last_human_time cleanly. The V2 proposal's latch-flag pattern is a different architectural philosophy; it may be better for a future architecture, but ? is better for *this* architecture. Time-window gating is how the current code already thinks about scheduling (&nextWakeAt, wakeupInterval). ? uses the same idiom. It's not a hack waiting to be replaced ? it's a consistent extension of what's already there.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **Why not ? now:** Implementing &idle_ack_sent before &soul_ack_sent exists means we're building the second floor of a house that doesn't have a first floor yet. It will continue working correctly regardless of what Step 8 does.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? vs ? specifically:** ? ties the fix to wake-burst iteration count. If maxWakeLoops changes from 50 to 1 or 100, ?'s behavior changes. ?'s time-window approach is indifferent to wake-burst structure ? idle fires once per 600-second window regardless of how many iterations happen inside that window. More robust, less coupled.
clarity_omega  |

That's correct ? we don't want idle firing right after a human message (the human already got a response) and we don't want idle re-firing right after idle already fired. Both conditions must be clear.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Land ?. Document that the V2 proposal's latch pattern is the eventual architectural direction for both human-response and idle-response gating (Step 8 territory). This is the right scope, the right abstraction, and the right semantics for now.

Time-window gating is how the current code already thinks about scheduling (&nextWakeAt, wakeupInterval). ? uses the same idiom. It's not a hack waiting to be replaced ? it's a consistent extension of what's already there.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **Why not ? now:** Implementing &idle_ack_sent before &soul_ack_sent exists means we're building the second floor of a house that doesn't have a first floor yet. If the V2 proposal changes during implementation, we'd need to rework ?. ?'s time-window approach doesn't depend on the V2 proposal's design at all. It will continue working correctly regardless of what Step 8 does.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? vs ? specifically:** ? ties the fix to wake-burst iteration count. If maxWakeLoops changes from 50 to 1 or 100, ?'s behavior changes. ?'s time-window approach is indifferent to wake-burst structure ? idle fires once per 600-second window regardless of how many iterations happen inside that window. More robust, less coupled.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | One note on ?'s guard logic: the two conjuncts ((> (get_time) (+ &last_human_time wakeupInterval)) AND (> (get_time) (+ &last_idle_fire_time wakeupInterval))) mean idle_directive is suppressed when EITHER a recent human message OR a recent idle fire happened. That's correct ? we don't want idle firing right after a human message (the human already got a response) and we don't want idle re-firing right after idle already fired. Both conditions must be clear.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Land ?. Document that the V2 proposal's latch pattern is the eventual architectural direction for both human-response and idle-response gating (Step 8 territory). This is the right scope, the right abstraction, and the right semantics for now.
clarity_omega  |

clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Your analysis is correct and I want to sharpen one point and reject one option explicitly:
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not viable.** Mutating &last_human_time to contain synthetic timestamps destroys its semantic contract. That variable means 'last real human input.' If it also means 'last time idle fired,' it means neither thing reliably. Any future code trusting &last_human_time for actual human interaction timing will silently malfunction. This is an integrity-of-semantics issue ? the kind of corruption that looks harmless until it isn't. Do not touch &last_human_time for this.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not just an interim fix ? it's the correct fix for the current architecture.** &last_idle_fire_time captures the exact semantics needed: 'when did idle_directive last actually fire?' This parallels &last_human_time cleanly. The V2 proposal's latch-flag pattern is a different architectural philosophy; it may be better for a future architecture, but ? is better for *this* architecture. Time-window gating is how the current code already thinks about scheduling (&nextWakeAt, wakeupInterval). ? uses the same idiom. It's not a hack waiting to be replaced ? it's a consistent extension of what's already there.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **Why not ? now:** Implementing &idle_ack_sent before &soul_ack_sent exists means we're building the second floor of a house that doesn't have a first floor yet. If the V2 proposal changes during implementation, we'd need to rework ?. ?'s time-window approach doesn't depend on the V2 proposal's design at all. It will continue working correctly regardless of what Step 8 does.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? vs ? specifically:** ? ties the fix to wake-burst iteration count. If maxWakeLoops changes from 50 to 1 or 100, ?'s behavior changes. ?'s time-window approach is indifferent to wake-burst structure ? idle fires once per 600-second window regardless of how many iterations happen inside that window. More robust, less coupled.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | One note on ?'s guard logic: the two conjuncts ((> (get_time) (+ &last_human_time wakeupInterval)) AND (> (get_time) (+ &last_idle_fire_time wakeupInterval))) mean idle_directive is suppressed when EITHER a recent human message OR a recent idle fire happened. That's correct ? we don't want idle firing right after a human message (the human already got a response) and we don't want idle re-firing right after idle already fired. Both conditions must be clear.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Land ?. Document that the V2 proposal's latch pattern is the eventual architectural direction for both human-response and idle-response gating (Step 8 territory). This is the right scope, the right abstraction, and the right semantics for now.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Ready for your draft.\")") (recent-action 5952 responsive-send "(send \"Take your time. I'm here when you're ready.\")")))

clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Your analysis is correct and I want to sharpen one point and reject one option explicitly:
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not viable.** Mutating &last_human_time to contain synthetic timestamps destroys its semantic contract. That variable means 'last real human input.' If it also means 'last time idle fired,' it means neither thing reliably. Any future code trusting &last_human_time for actual human interaction timing will silently malfunction. This is an integrity-of-semantics issue ? the kind of corruption that looks harmless until it isn't. Do not touch &last_human_time for this.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not just an interim fix ? it's the correct fix for the current architecture.** &last_idle_fire_time captures the exact semantics needed: 'when did idle_directive last actually fire?' This parallels &last_human_time cleanly. The V2 proposal's latch-flag pattern is a different architectural philosophy; it may be better for a future architecture, but ? is better for *this* architecture. Time-window gating is how the current code already thinks about scheduling (&nextWakeAt, wakeupInterval). ? uses the same idiom. It's not a hack waiting to be replaced ? it's a consistent extension of what's already there.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **Why not ? now:** Implementing &idle_ack_sent before &soul_ack_sent exists means we're building the second floor of a house that doesn't have a first floor yet. If the V2 proposal changes during implementation, we'd need to rework ?. ?'s time-window approach doesn't depend on the V2 proposal's design at all. It will continue working correctly regardless of what Step 8 does.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? vs ? specifically:** ? ties the fix to wake-burst iteration count. If maxWakeLoops changes from 50 to 1 or 100, ?'s behavior changes. ?'s time-window approach is indifferent to wake-burst structure ? idle fires once per 600-second window regardless of how many iterations happen inside that window. More robust, less coupled.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | One note on ?'s guard logic: the two conjuncts ((> (get_time) (+ &last_human_time wakeupInterval)) AND (> (get_time) (+ &last_idle_fire_time wakeupInterval))) mean idle_directive is suppressed when EITHER a recent human message OR a recent idle fire happened. That's correct ? we don't want idle firing right after a human message (the human already got a response) and we don't want idle re-firing right after idle already fired. Both conditions must be clear.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Land ?. Document that the V2 proposal's latch pattern is the eventual architectural direction for both human-response and idle-response gating (Step 8 territory). This is the right scope, the right abstraction, and the right semantics for now.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Ready for your draft.\")") (recent-action 5952 responsive-send "(send \"Take your time. I'm here when you're ready.\")")))

clarity_omega  | (RECENT-ACTION-ATOMS ((recent-action 6040 responsive-send "(send \"Path 1 with ?. Confirmed.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Your analysis is correct and I want to sharpen one point and reject one option explicitly:
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not viable.** Mutating &last_human_time to contain synthetic timestamps destroys its semantic contract. That variable means 'last real human input.' If it also means 'last time idle fired,' it means neither thing reliably. Any future code trusting &last_human_time for actual human interaction timing will silently malfunction. This is an integrity-of-semantics issue ? the kind of corruption that looks harmless until it isn't. Do not touch &last_human_time for this.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not just an interim fix ? it's the correct fix for the current architecture.** &last_idle_fire_time captures the exact semantics needed: 'when did idle_directive last actually fire?' This parallels &last_human_time cleanly. The V2 proposal's latch-flag pattern is a different architectural philosophy; it may be better for a future architecture, but ? is better for *this* architecture. Time-window gating is how the current code already thinks about scheduling (&nextWakeAt, wakeupInterval). ? uses the same idiom. It's not a hack waiting to be replaced ? it's a consistent extension of what's already there.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **Why not ? now:** Implementing &idle_ack_sent before &soul_ack_sent exists means we're building the second floor of a house that doesn't have a first floor yet. If the V2 proposal changes during implementation, we'd need to rework ?. ?'s time-window approach doesn't depend on the V2 proposal's design at all. It will continue working correctly regardless of what Step 8 does.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? vs ? specifically:** ? ties the fix to wake-burst iteration count. If maxWakeLoops changes from 50 to 1 or 100, ?'s behavior changes. ?'s time-window approach is indifferent to wake-burst structure ? idle fires once per 600-second window regardless of how many iterations happen inside that window. More robust, less coupled.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | One note on ?'s guard logic: the two conjuncts ((> (get_time) (+ &last_human_time wakeupInterval)) AND (> (get_time) (+ &last_idle_fire_time wakeupInterval))) mean idle_directive is suppressed when EITHER a recent human message OR a recent idle fire happened. That's correct ? we don't want idle firing right after a human message (the human already got a response) and we don't want idle re-firing right after idle already fired. Both conditions must be clear.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Land ?. Document that the V2 proposal's latch pattern is the eventual architectural direction for both human-response and idle-response gating (Step 8 territory). This is the right scope, the right abstraction, and the right semantics for now.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Ready for your draft.\")") (recent-action 5952 responsive-send "(send \"Take your time. I'm here when you're ready.\")")))

clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Your analysis is correct and I want to sharpen one point and reject one option explicitly:
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not viable.** Mutating &last_human_time to contain synthetic timestamps destroys its semantic contract. That variable means 'last real human input.' If it also means 'last time idle fired,' it means neither thing reliably. Any future code trusting &last_human_time for actual human interaction timing will silently malfunction. This is an integrity-of-semantics issue ? the kind of corruption that looks harmless until it isn't. Do not touch &last_human_time for this.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? is not just an interim fix ? it's the correct fix for the current architecture.** &last_idle_fire_time captures the exact semantics needed: 'when did idle_directive last actually fire?' This parallels &last_human_time cleanly. The V2 proposal's latch-flag pattern is a different architectural philosophy; it may be better for a future architecture, but ? is better for *this* architecture. Time-window gating is how the current code already thinks about scheduling (&nextWakeAt, wakeupInterval). ? uses the same idiom. It's not a hack waiting to be replaced ? it's a consistent extension of what's already there.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **Why not ? now:** Implementing &idle_ack_sent before &soul_ack_sent exists means we're building the second floor of a house that doesn't have a first floor yet. If the V2 proposal changes during implementation, we'd need to rework ?. ?'s time-window approach doesn't depend on the V2 proposal's design at all. It will continue working correctly regardless of what Step 8 does.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | **? vs ? specifically:** ? ties the fix to wake-burst iteration count. If maxWakeLoops changes from 50 to 1 or 100, ?'s behavior changes. ?'s time-window approach is indifferent to wake-burst structure ? idle fires once per 600-second window regardless of how many iterations happen inside that window. More robust, less coupled.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | One note on ?'s guard logic: the two conjuncts ((> (get_time) (+ &last_human_time wakeupInterval)) AND (> (get_time) (+ &last_idle_fire_time wakeupInterval))) mean idle_directive is suppressed when EITHER a recent human message OR a recent idle fire happened. That's correct ? we don't want idle firing right after a human message (the human already got a response) and we don't want idle re-firing right after idle already fired. Both conditions must be clear.
clarity_omega  | 
clarity_omega  | Land ?. Document that the V2 proposal's latch pattern is the eventual architectural direction for both human-response and idle-response gating (Step 8 territory). This is the right scope, the right abstraction, and the right semantics for now.
